  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_663b1a95-67c1-4302-842d-34eedcd96e9b'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1397253716244014704">Far beneath the surface of the earth, upon the shores of the Starless Sea, there is a labyrinthine collection of tunnels and rooms filled with stories. The entryways that lead to this sanctuary are often hidden, sometimes on forest floors, sometimes in private homes, sometimes in plain sight. But those who seek will find. Their doors have been waiting for them.<br/><br/>Zachary Ezra</span>
  <span id="freeText1397253716244014704" style="display:none">Far beneath the surface of the earth, upon the shores of the Starless Sea, there is a labyrinthine collection of tunnels and rooms filled with stories. The entryways that lead to this sanctuary are often hidden, sometimes on forest floors, sometimes in private homes, sometimes in plain sight. But those who seek will find. Their doors have been waiting for them.<br /><br />Zachary Ezra Rawlins is searching for his door, though he does not know it. He follows a silent siren song, an inexplicable knowledge that he is meant for another place. When he discovers a mysterious book in the stacks of his campus library he begins to read, entranced by tales of lovelorn prisoners, lost cities, and nameless acolytes. Suddenly a turn of the page brings Zachary to a story from his own childhood impossibly written in this book that is older than he is.<br /><br />A bee, a key, and a sword emblazoned on the book lead Zachary to two people who will change the course of his life: Mirabel, a fierce, pink-haired painter, and Dorian, a handsome, barefoot man with shifting alliances. These strangers guide Zachary through masquerade party dances and whispered back room stories to the headquarters of a secret society where doorknobs hang from ribbons, and finally through a door conjured from paint to the place he has always yearned for. Amid twisting tunnels filled with books, gilded ballrooms, and wine-dark shores Zachary falls into an intoxicating world soaked in romance and mystery. But a battle is raging over the fate of this place and though there are those who would willingly sacrifice everything to protect it, there are just as many intent on its destruction. As Zachary, Mirabel, and Dorian venture deeper into the space and its histories and myths, searching for answers and each other, a timeless love story unspools, casting a spell of pirates, painters, lovers, liars, and ships that sail upon a Starless Sea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1397253716244014704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

//]]>
</script>    </div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2913818259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2913818259" />
    <a title="Lisa Lynch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35364873-lisa-lynch"><img alt="Lisa Lynch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567203905p2/35364873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2913818259?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Lynch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Lynch" href="/user/show/35364873-lisa-lynch">Lisa Lynch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2913818259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15041186775511752254"><blockquote>"How are you feeling?" Zachary asks.<br/><br/>"Like I am losing my mind, but in a slow, achingly beautiful sort of way." (p.288)</blockquote><br/><br/>Funny, I felt the exact same way while reading this book. <br/><br/>So, Erin Morgenstern's The Starless Sea is the highly anticipated follow up to The Night Circus (which, I admit, I haven't read). I won an ARC of this book from my library's summer reading program and, after reading the synopsis, I could not wait to jump in. <br/><br/>I think that most people who read The Starless Sea will love it b</span>
  <span id="freeText15041186775511752254" style="display:none"><blockquote>"How are you feeling?" Zachary asks.<br /><br />"Like I am losing my mind, but in a slow, achingly beautiful sort of way." (p.288)</blockquote><br /><br />Funny, I felt the exact same way while reading this book. <br /><br />So, Erin Morgenstern's The Starless Sea is the highly anticipated follow up to The Night Circus (which, I admit, I haven't read). I won an ARC of this book from my library's summer reading program and, after reading the synopsis, I could not wait to jump in. <br /><br />I think that most people who read The Starless Sea will love it because it's a love letter to storytelling. If you like literature, there is a good chance you will enjoy this book. <br /><br />I was <i>sure</i> I would enjoy it too. I mean, The Starless Sea seemed like it was written just for me. We have a protagonist who studies video games and reads a lot and is near-sighted. There are books and cats and keys and bees and so many stories... <br /><br />But, sadly, I am here to say I was incredibly underwhelmed and disappointed by this book.<br /><br />Here's why:<br /><br /><b>1) I had no idea what was going on for the majority of this book.</b> I do not feel that this is due to my own ineptitude. But rather, I didn't know what was going on in this book because nothing was going on. People who love Morgenstern's writing and love works that pay homage to literature might overlook this. Unfortunately, I could not.<br /><br />The Starless Sea starts with a fascinating inciting incident. This guy named Zachary finds an old book at his library that tells <i>his</i> story. On a quest to discover why this book tells his story, Zachary soon finds himself in this magical library/world with some magical people. What follows is a series of seemingly endless fish-out-of-water scenes as Zachary bumbles along, trying to make sense of this magical place.<br /><br />But even when things started to "come together" in the last 100 pages or so, I still felt like I had no idea what was going on. I constantly asked "but what is the point?" while reading this book and never, even at the end, got a satisfactory answer. <br /><br /><u>The Starless Sea is almost a retelling of Alice in Wonderland... except that Alice had an end goal and didn't need to fall in love to get there.</u> <br /><br />But seriously. Imagine if Alice fell down the rabbit hole into Wonderland then never tried to get back home because she was too busy just looking around and fantasizing about the Mad Hatter. And there you have the "plot" of The Starless Sea.<br /><br /><b>2) There is no plot.</b> I'm confounded by this book, and not because of the richly imaginative world it is set in. I'm confounded by the lack of any narrative structure. THIS BOOK IS A LOVE LETTER TO STORYTELLING THAT FORGOT TO HAVE THAT WHICH EVERY STORY NEEDS: A PLOT! The only thing propelling Zachary forward in this story is the story itself. His motivations are unclear and his actions are minimal at best. <br /><br />Here is the closest thing we get to an explanation as to why Zachary didn't just go home from the start:<br /><br /><blockquote><i>What are you doing?</i> a voice in his head asks an he doesn't have a good answer for it. Doesn't know what or why or even where, exactly, because he forgot to check the street sign on the corner. He could keep walking, hail a cab, return to his hotel. But he wants his book back. And he wants to know what happens next. (p.87)</blockquote><br /><br />So Zachary goes down the rabbit hole just because he wants to see what happens next?? Ok fine I guess. I was on board with this for the first 100 pages. But then 200 pages roll around and then 300... And eventually I got 400 pages in and honestly considered throwing the book out the window. A purpose other than "to see what happens next" is NEVER revealed. <u>The purpose of this story was to get to the end. I'm not kidding!</u><br /><br />At one point, this conversation occurs:<br /><br /><blockquote>"I remain here because it is my job, Mister Rawlins. My calling, my duty, my raison d'etre. Why are you here?"<br /><br /><i>Because a book said I was supposed to be,</i> Zachary thinks. <i>Because I'm worried about going back... Because I feel more alive down here than I did up there.</i><br /><br />"I'm here to sail the Starless Sea and breathe the haunted air," he says. (p.234)</blockquote><br /><br />While this might sound beautiful, there is nothing behind it. Zachary is compelled forward in this story by destiny and curiosity and I hate to say it, but that just isn't enough. <u>There needed to be something more to this book than beautiful descriptions of a magical world.</u><br /><br />I kept waiting for <i>something</i> to happen. And things happened I guess, but they all seemed circumstantial and nonsensical. Zachary is the most passive protagonist I've ever come across. He kind of just wanders around marveling at the strangeness of the world he is in. Everything felt incredibly contrived and convenient. I can only suspend my disbelief for so long.<br /><br /><b>3) There was no antagonist or central conflict.</b> Again, I'm utterly confounded. What publishers and editors read this book and agreed to print it?? Without a plot and without a conflict, what do we have?? Dreams. Fragments. <br /><br /><u>I know people have been waiting like 8 years for another book by Morgenstern, but come one. I'm struggling with calling this a book!</u><br /><br />There is this "bad" lady named Allegra but she has like two scenes in the whole book and isn't really a threat. And as far as conflict goes, the biggest "problem" is that Zachary (and me as a reader) has no idea what is going on. He has nobody to defeat and nothing to overcome. So what is the point of his "journey"?? TO FALL IN LOVE?? GET TF OUT OF HERE!!<br /><br /><b>4) The main story is interrupted every other chapter and it drove me crazy.</b> So this book alternates between Zachary's main quest line and these little flash-fiction-like stories. Later in the book, the main quest is broken up by perspective shifts. I get why all this stuff was there and I did appreciate it, but it was so overwhelming. It was very hard for me to keep everything straight in my head. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed some of the stories but, my god, there was just too much. Zachary's story was interesting in the beginning, but once I realized there was no plot and everything that happened was just a series of events, I began to lose interest. I would forget where I left off with Zachary, so it made it hard to want to continue reading. With 100 pages left out of this 500 page book, I honestly thought about not finishing it. <br /><br /><b>5) The characters are underdeveloped.</b> Zachary Ezra Rawlins is kind of a blank slate. I get that readers are supposed to relate to him and even insert themselves into this story through him, but the guy is just kind of... dull. Mirabel, Dorian, The Keeper, Allegra... they were all dull. I didn't care about any of them. There was better characterization in some of the interrupting stories than there was in the main quest (notice I'm not using the word "plot" here because THERE WAS NO PLOT.)<br /><br />The only character that kind of has a character arc is... well shit. None of them. <u>None of these characters, despite journeying through this magical world, change. There is no personal growth or enlightenment. They don't even come across many challenges other than ignorance and bewilderment.</u><br /><br /><b>6) This book is bogged down by long, tedious descriptions of the setting.</b> I have a confession. I was so sick and tired of this book that I began skipping the paragraphs that described the setting in the last 100 pages. And, you know what? It got incredibly more readable. I didn't realize it until then, but all of these overlong descriptions were basically purposeless. They were there to be aesthetic and to look cool.<br /><br />I think this book would have benefited from having like 200 pages trimmed out of it. Get rid of all these endless descriptions and remove like half of the interrupting stories and perspective shifts. Add in some character development and a whole lot of plot... Then there might be something to work with. In all honesty, this book could have been amazing. <br /><br /><b>7) The romance is unbelievable and stupid.</b> I didn't buy Zachary and Dorian's relationship for a second. They kind of saved each other's lives once or twice, but never had any time to develop a deep connection. They spent an evening drinking wine and reading together, (and by "reading together" I mean reading different books in the same room together) but had no other significant interactions. They never flirted or talked to each other more than a few sentences. Then all of a sudden Dorian grabs Zachary's head and whispers:<br /><br /><blockquote>"I need you to know that what I feel for you is real. Because I think you feel the same. I have lost a lot of things and I don't want to lose this too." (p.312)</blockquote><br /><br />Uh, what??!? At this point in the book, I wasn't even sure that Dorian was gay and <i>liked</i> Zachary, let alone was in love with him. It is hinted at that Zachary and Dorian are meant to be together because of some prophetic nonsense, but my god. Throw some scenes of them getting to know each other so that I believe they are in love. This is also the sexiest moment between the two in the whole book and that's pretty sad. <br /><br /><b>8) This book feels like it needs to be read twice to fully understand and enjoy.</b> I wholeheartedly resent this. It was hard enough for me to finish this book the first time. I will never read it again.<br /><br /><br />So, in order to be fair, I guess I should mention the good things about this book. Some of these "positives" are going to end up being backhanded compliments, but I'm over worrying about it. I DIDN'T LIKE THIS BOOK THAT MUCH, so I'm grasping at straws here.<br /><br /><br /><b>1) The world in The Starless Sea is fascinating.</b> I loved the aesthetics of it. This book is full to the brim with fantastic imagery. I loved that this world of stories was filled with keys, cats, books, and a boatload of mystery. It was such a goddamn shame that all this cool imagery was overused and purposeless.<br /><br />If you can get past all the highfalutin metaphors, similes, and imagery, there is a very interesting, unique world made up of stories. How freaking cool to have a world that is basically a perpetual story? Like, the stories end, but one follows to take its place.<br /><br /><b>2) The writing is beautiful.</b> Morgenstern's prose is very dreamlike and poetic. It is too bad what was written lacked an overall purpose, message, and plot. I think this book needed a heavier editing hand and maybe a bit more time in the oven. It is clearly undercooked. <br /><br />I rated Erin Morgenstern's The Starless Sea 3 out of 5 stars.<br /><br />**Update** So I've been thinking about this book for like a week or so and I'm dropping my rating to 2 stars. My frustration with this book really got to me. While finishing up the last 100 pages of The Starless Sea, I realized that I was incredibly grumpy. It was negatively impacting my life and I should have gone with my gut and thrown the damn thing out the window.<br /><br />I ended up finishing this book, despite my urge to chuck it into the bushes, because I felt it was important for someone to be the voice of reason. I wanted to point out the flaws and problems. I have a feeling this book will end up being very highly rated here on Goodreads for 2 reasons:<br /><br />1: This book panders to its audience by having a protagonist that is designed to appeal to readers. He is nerdy, near-sighted, part of a minority group, and he likes video games, books, and cats. This book also panders to its audience by referencing literary works.<br /><br />2: The Starless Sea will ride the coattails of The Night Circus. People who loved TNC will love TSS.<br /><br />I don't recommend this book.<br /><br />**I read an ARC of this book, so quotes and page numbers might end up being changed in the final product.**</span>
  <a data-text-id="15041186775511752254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2588019754" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2588019754?book_show_action=true">Nov 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781910701454" href="/book/show/42730332-the-starless-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-mm">lgbtq-mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-slow-burn">trope-slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-doomed-tragic-love">trope-doomed-tragic-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-gay-yearning">trope-gay-yearning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2588019754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4376051491771405929">✧ <a href='https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com/2019/09/29/review-the-starless-sea-by-erin-morgenstern/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>find this review & others on my blog</b>
</a> ✧<br/><br/>It’s a profoundly strange thing—to feel as though you are wading through mildly entertaining novels that pass through you like falling smoke, always searching for the one that reaches into the back alleys of your soul and settles to the bottom of you like fallen leaves.<br/><br/><b>And then there it is, like a faint spark bobbing on a dark sea, calling you, beckoning.</b><br/><br/>The bliss of it is like what all the books you’ve ever read have been aspiring to be, the scales of</span>
  <span id="freeText4376051491771405929" style="display:none">✧ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com/2019/09/29/review-the-starless-sea-by-erin-morgenstern/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>find this review &amp; others on my blog</b>
</a> ✧<br /><br />It’s a profoundly strange thing—to feel as though you are wading through mildly entertaining novels that pass through you like falling smoke, always searching for the one that reaches into the back alleys of your soul and settles to the bottom of you like fallen leaves.<br /><br /><b>And then there it is, like a faint spark bobbing on a dark sea, calling you, beckoning.</b><br /><br />The bliss of it is like what all the books you’ve ever read have been aspiring to be, the scales of what is good, great, and transcendent recalibrating in your head. The story that is a door creaking open in your chest, pouring light into that unyielding hollowness. A secret burning like a lantern in the center of you. Something you could crawl into if only you <em>believed</em> it hard enough.<br /><br />To borrow some of Morgenstern’s words, “<em>books are always better when read rather than explained</em>.” Words fall short of this marvel, but I want you to read this book, so I had to try.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“For those who feel homesick for a place they’ve never been to. Those who seek even if they do not know what (or where) it is that they are seeking. Those who seek will find. Their doors have been waiting for them.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />A subterranean library where reality can be shuffled like a deck of cards—a drunken mangle of past and present. Stories that wander off the edge of the page, filled with teeth and armored with immortality. People who wander off the edge of the map,  perilously and fathomlessly free, the unnameable future ahead of them—endless reams of blank paper. And the secret society undoing it all, unwinding the Starless Sea thread by thread, until it falls away.<br /><br />And in the center of it all: Zachary Ezra Rawlins.<br /><br />This is Erin Morgernstern’s much-anticipated second novel. The basics, at least. The <em>bones</em>. But stories—as stories often do—grow in the telling:<br /><br />Zachary Ezra Rawlins stumbled across an authorless book in the library, and in the deepest, most unshakable part of himself where reason was useless, he knew without a doubt that it was narrating a long-ago event of his childhood. Back when 11-year-old Zachary found a painted door, unknowingly teetering on the invisible edge of a great cliff, but held himself back from the seething, teeming sea below. The door (and the unspoken invitation) was gone the next day, like a wave washing clean over sand.<br /><br />But here was a second chance, a do-over, and Zachary clung to it with the self-propelling recklessness of hope's last effort. The scattered uncertainties of his youth fell away. This was the unwritten story, still swelling in its hollows, breathing tendrils of magic into the air. But there’s a strange darkening, something nameless hanging on the horizon. Soon, dreams and nightmares start borrowing each other’s faces, and Zachary’s time is as sands running through an hourglass grain by grain.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“I think people came here for the same reason we came here,” Dorian says. “In search of something. Even if we didn’t know what it was. Something more. Something to wonder at. Someplace to belong. <strong>We’re here to wander through other people’s stories, searching for our own.”</strong></em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em>The Starless Sea</em> is a love letter to those of us dogged with the invisible burden of unbelonging that stirs us from the stillness and sends us out into the page in search of solace, those of us who carry stories like a secret talisman in our pockets and rub words for comfort until they are worn smooth as creek stones, those of us who once turned away from our own painted doors before we took courage and learned to feel the surge of fear and stifle it.<br /><br />Emerging after 8 years—like a glittering literary cicada—with a remarkably powerful novel, Morgenstern holds our gaze for the space of a few hundred pages and fills it with what she wills.<br /><br />The author’s imagination is keener than almost anyone's. Her pen has a heart inside and warmth as fire does, and it plucked a string in me, every line coming forth like a note of music—drenched with meaning, spangled and thundering with it. Hers is prose that lingers in the blood, lit like a coal in your belly. A story that attaches itself, ravenously, to its readers, long after the words have run out.<br /><br />With exacting precision while giving the impression of effortlessness, Morgenstern engineers a recklessly splendid plot.. There are tales layered upon tales and characters free to wander, leaving their books to taste life in other stories. It all meshes together quite immaculately. The multiples narratives are connected by crisscrossing threads of character and plot, and Morgenstern balances upon them like a tightrope walker, dashing from page to page. As dizzying as it gets, she never once slips.<br /><br />Morgenstern has truly invented her own brand of page-turner. As much as I wanted to sit back and luxuriate over the sumptuously varnished prose, I kept going, going, going, chasing after every sentence as if the words themselves were on horseback, wild and furious, racing after the riddles of Fate and Time, of pirates and tongueless acolytes, of weary travelers and wearier lovers, of foretelling sculptors and all-seeing Owls, before getting swept out by a rogue wave to the Starless Sea, swimming against riptides, finally staggering ashore to a landscape you couldn’t begin to make sense of yet still as familiar as the remembrance of a touch.<br /><br /><strong>But this novel is, above all, a love story—one that shone like light upon the waves of the Starless Sea, dazzling to blindness.</strong> Zachary and Dorian’s love tale was sometimes as fierce as joy, and sometimes like a knife blade pressed to my flesh. A held gaze in a sea of stares sliding past you as though you didn’t exist and you two are the only fixed points in a universe of motion. His voice like a phantom feather over skin—<em>a storyteller’s voice</em>—and his presence like a rope thrown into a churning sea. This person that is “<em>a place you could lose yourself in, and never wish to be found</em>,” as familiar as one's own skin. This frenzied, fevered need to know one another. A love story you’ll want a return ticket to.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>“And no story ever truly ends as long as it is told.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><strong>Reader,<em> The Starless Sea</em> is a door standing open before you—step into it and let it step into you.</strong><br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/proyearner" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="4376051491771405929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2588322804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17296491288731751781">Yes, I teared up upon finishing my reread of this book like a starlet in an old movie. No, I don't want to talk about it. <s>I JUST WANT THIS TO NEVER END.</s><br/><br/>a lovely little reread with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10148904-lily' rel='nofollow noopener'>lily</a><br/><br/>-------------<br/><br/>Someone PLEASE procure me a striking, modern, big-city apartment with lots of windows, where I can hold a glass of expensive wine and gaze unseeing over the skyline at night, because apparently I’m going to feel melancholy for the rest of my life over never again being able to read this for the first t</span>
  <span id="freeText17296491288731751781" style="display:none">Yes, I teared up upon finishing my reread of this book like a starlet in an old movie. No, I don't want to talk about it. <s>I JUST WANT THIS TO NEVER END.</s><br /><br />a lovely little reread with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10148904-lily" rel="nofollow noopener">lily</a><br /><br />-------------<br /><br />Someone PLEASE procure me a striking, modern, big-city apartment with lots of windows, where I can hold a glass of expensive wine and gaze unseeing over the skyline at night, because apparently I’m going to feel melancholy for the rest of my life over never again being able to read this for the first time and if I’m going to do so I at least want to be glamorous about it.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2020/03/14/my-favorite-books-of-the-whole-year-only-3-months-late/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />Or, at the very least, I need to locate the sort of old-fashioned library described in 1920s mystery novels with a bar cart stocked with aged scotch and shelves filled with leather-bound tomes, except their antique spines will be a façade for the kinds of things I actually enjoy reading, rather than being 800 different copies of the Bible or whatever, and I will never drink the scotch because everything about the process of drinking scotch is like the scotch is asking you not to drink it. (Scotch is the poison-dart frog of beverages.)<br /><br />Basically what I’m saying here is - Ever since I read the last page of this book three months ago, I have felt a small, unrelenting sadness, which I believe will only be solved by one of the following methods:<br />a) I dedicate my life to tracking down a door to the Starless Sea, and either I find one or it turns out the real reward was the friends I made along the way;<br />b) I experience repeated memory loss, allowing myself to read this book over and over again for the first time, re-beginning every time I finish it;<br />or c) I live the rest of my days in homage to this story.<br /><br />All options will require funds that I will never have (I’m an English major, after all), so please kindly Venmo me at your convenience. Thanks.<br /><br />This is the most gorgeous ode to stories and literature. It’s a thank-you gift to anyone who has ever been a Reader, with a capital R - not just someone who reads but someone WHO READS, as an identity, as a life-force, as a passion, as the meaning of life. <br /><br />I dare any true bookworm to read this book with an open heart and a ready mind and not feel grateful that their life overlapped with its publication date.<br /><br />Erin Morgenstern’s ability to create divine settings you can see and smell and lust after and yearn to experience is unparalleled. <br /><br />My favorite book ever is, as anyone who has so much as made the online equivalent of eye contact me knows, Alice’s Adventures in Wonderland. I love it with enough passion that everything about it is my favorite of that thing: my favorite characters, my favorite prose, and, naturally, my favorite setting.<br /><br />Before I read this book, my unrivaled first runner-up was the setting of the Night Circus. <br /><br />Now, I think both Wonderland and the circus may have been bumped down a slot. Never has a setting known me, seen my soul, like that of the magical underground great world of stories in these pages.<br /><br />Plus, I didn’t have to slog through a Night Circus-level instalove romance to get there.<br /><br />This was a perfect book. Mysterious, confusing, strange, magical. Beautifully written and populated with characters you love hard and immediately. I read this so slowly because I SAVORED it. I, a compulsive speed-reader whose simultaneous highest compliment and M.O. is reading a book in a day or so, knew that my finishing this book would be a small heartbreak, and so I tried to postpone it as long as I could.<br /><br />So instead, I’ll pay the highest compliment to this that any reader can pay to any story - <br /><br />Bottom line: It was hard to pick up another book after reading this one.<br /><br />-------------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />i wanted this to never ever ever end ever.<br /><br />the fact that it did is my biggest complaint.<br /><br />review to come / 5 stars<br /><br />-------------<br /><i>currently reading updates</i><br /><br />i hope someday i love something as much as erin morgenstern loves comma splices<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />me: i need to finish my reading challenge!!!<br /><br />also me: (picks up 500-page book)<br /><br />-------------<br /><i>tbr review</i><br /><br />wait.........MULTIPLE beautiful covers????<br /><br />someone take mercy on me<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />COVERCOVERCOVERCOVERCOVERCOVERCOVERCOVER!!!<br /><br />-------------<br /><br />hello i would like to read this now please. 2019 is not going to work for me thank you</span>

<div id="review_2993675564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2993675564" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2993675564?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780593106488" href="/book/show/43671440-the-starless-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10171516-jessica?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2993675564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4264223364239193730">HAPPY PUBLICATION DAY TO THIS LITTLE COCKTAIL OF MAGIC AND WONDER!<br/><br/>i know for a fact that this book wont be everyones cup of tea (morgensterns writing style is an acquired taste), but it sure is mine. <br/><br/>this quenches my thirst for a story that was meant to be told, a love letter to the art of storytelling, as well as the stories we find ourselves in. it is an ode to those who write their own paths in life. and there is an aromatic intimacy to this that can only be created when such words are so ten</span>
  <span id="freeText4264223364239193730" style="display:none">HAPPY PUBLICATION DAY TO THIS LITTLE COCKTAIL OF MAGIC AND WONDER!<br /><br />i know for a fact that this book wont be everyones cup of tea (morgensterns writing style is an acquired taste), but it sure is mine. <br /><br />this quenches my thirst for a story that was meant to be told, a love letter to the art of storytelling, as well as the stories we find ourselves in. it is an ode to those who write their own paths in life. and there is an aromatic intimacy to this that can only be created when such words are so tenderly placed on a page. <br /><br />with delicious notes of myth and legend, imagination and wonder, this supplies the perfect blend of magic, bravery, adventure, wisdom, and love. it is a full-bodied flavour that impacts the palate, leaving it satiated, yet somehow desiring more. <br /><br />this is a story to be savoured from one page to the next, entincing the reader to acknowledge all the smooth layers and undertones, because each word has such a meaningful presence, it would be a shame to miss something. <br /><br />and as i drink up every last letter, i become so delightfully intoxicated on the notion that we are all made of stories and stardust. its a buzzed feeling that reminds me exactly why i fell in love with reading in the first place and how we all become a part of the stories we love. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <blockquote>
    <blockquote>
      <blockquote>
        <blockquote>🐝 🗝 🗡</blockquote>
      </blockquote>
    </blockquote>
  </blockquote>
</blockquote><br /><b>↠ <i>every star to return to the starless sea</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4264223364239193730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10595472600551813240">I waited the book for months and months, also named myself as Vladimir who is waiting for Godot forever! Of course my request stays at the NetGalley limbo space with other thousands of my requests doing boogie dance together. (I don’t want to visualize them dusted, positioned at the bookshelves kind of purgatory!) So as a patient reading, high five-d myself for releasing day (actually I slapped my nose, I couldn’t do a proper high five for years and always missing the other person’s hand or alwa</span>
  <span id="freeText10595472600551813240" style="display:none">I waited the book for months and months, also named myself as Vladimir who is waiting for Godot forever! Of course my request stays at the NetGalley limbo space with other thousands of my requests doing boogie dance together. (I don’t want to visualize them dusted, positioned at the bookshelves kind of purgatory!) So as a patient reading, high five-d myself for releasing day (actually I slapped my nose, I couldn’t do a proper high five for years and always missing the other person’s hand or always find them on my face!!!!)<br /><br /> Reading this book is seeing a dream into dream into dream. I felt like jumped into full throttle triple time intensive Inception universe. (So I visualized most of the book’s characters as Leo and Tom which made my day and give me an amazing selfie smile all day long!) So you’re reading amazing story about intertwined magical stories. It’s a mind-bending brain storming process because narrator jumps between stories and your grey cells get used to run marathons to catch where the main story goes and gather the crumbles left for you like Hansel and Gretel. <br /><br />But I have to admit at the final you find better place than a house made of sweets (Yes, I actually found my fountain of Chardonnay when I caught the simple rhythm of the stories. Let’ drink to that!) But I still feel the smoke coming out of my ears because this kind of brain gymnastic has side effect like over exhaustion and dismantle the rest of remaining brain cells. Luckily I know the feeling because I read too many Blake Crouch books that make me prepare this kind of mind-blowing experience. I like challenges! Bring it on!<br /><br />I also have to admit Morgenstern is a magician. She can bend words, add different meanings, put a lyrical touch to enchant you. Just like Night Circus, the same thing happened to me. I hear a wonderful symphony in my head and waltz in my room, remembering those intriguing, magical stories you want to keep reading. Even the book is too long, you don’t want to stop flipping pages and get lost in those creatively depicted universes and of course you never get bored and enjoy each second of your experience.<br />Did I like it? NOOOOOO!!! I LOVEEEEDDDD IT SOOOO MUCCCHHH( I’m screaming right now but thankfully you can only sense my excitement from the big caps and wrong grammar usage :) )<br /><br />And don’t forget to enjoy every words about heartwarming, tempting love tale of Zachary and Dorian. It’s not about modern love it is about to find the person reminds you a place you could lose yourself in and never wish to be found. DEEP SIGH. Yes. I truly love it. Period!<br /><br /><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br /><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br /><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>

<div id="review_2589781803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2589781803" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2589781803?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781910701454" href="/book/show/42730332-the-starless-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2589781803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15371112276737173755"><b>
  <u>This is a review I did not want to write because this is a book I so desperately wanted to love. </u>
</b><br/><br/><i>The Starless Sea</i> is a book written for true readers. I’m talking about the kind of person who spent their childhood in and out of libraries and bookshops; the kind of person who sits and imagines adventure and an escape from the mundaneness of every single endless day without magic: the kind of person who <i>lives</i> for books and reading. <br/><br/>As such it is totally enchanting to begin with it. It hooks you</span>
  <span id="freeText15371112276737173755" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>This is a review I did not want to write because this is a book I so desperately wanted to love. </u>
</b><br /><br /><i>The Starless Sea</i> is a book written for true readers. I’m talking about the kind of person who spent their childhood in and out of libraries and bookshops; the kind of person who sits and imagines adventure and an escape from the mundaneness of every single endless day without magic: the kind of person who <i>lives</i> for books and reading. <br /><br />As such it is totally enchanting to begin with it. It hooks you in and will promise you storytelling delights, but these promises are false and lead to absolutely nothing but disappointment because the story will lose itself and collapse inward: it will fail in a spectacularly miserable fashion. And it is tragic because this book has been an exceptionally long time in the making. It needed a better editor to polish this lump of rock into the diamond it ought to have been. <br /><br /><b>So, do I think <i>The Starless Sea</i> could have been a good book?</b><br /><br /> Absolutely. What it needed was time, refinement, and a great deal of editing. The prose is written superbly; however, the structure of the book is a complete narrative mess that goes nowhere and becomes terribly confusing as it collapses on itself and forgets the very purpose of storytelling: to tell a story, not simply beguile with pretty words and cool fantasy elements. There needs to be a purpose. <br /><br />I make no reservation in claiming that this book could have been as effective as Gaiman’s masterpiece <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15783514-the-ocean-at-the-end-of-the-lane?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=wwqSvuEj6w&amp;rank=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ocean at the End of the Lane</a>. It seriously had that much potential, but it was wasted. And I'm angry, bitter and frustrated because I do not want to write these words. I want to celebrate what this book could have been, not lament what it was not.<br /><br />I suppose two stars will have to do for this brilliantly enchanting book that wasted everything it had and failed to deliver what it promised. <br /><br />_________________________________<br /><br />You can connect with me on social media via <a href="https://linktr.ee/sean.ultra_vegan1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Linktree</a>.<br />__________________________________</span>
  <a data-text-id="15371112276737173755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3587064693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3587064693" />
    <a title="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58160628-emily-books-with-emily-fox"><img alt="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546189365p2/58160628.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3587064693?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" href="/user/show/58160628-emily-books-with-emily-fox">Emily (Books with Emily Fox)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385686228" href="/book/show/43658908-the-starless-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58160628-emily-books-with-emily-fox?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3587064693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17775871239831219327">Read this as part of my "Giving authors a second/last chance" challenge and...<br/><br/>This is a tough one for me. <br/><br/>I can acknowledge that Morgenstern’s writing is whimsical but after two books by her leaving me confused and unsatisfied, I have to admit her books are simply not for me.<br/><br/>The worlds she creates are fascinating but I don't find myself caring enough about the story in them nor the characters. Frankly, I felt bored.<br/><br/>If you've enjoyed The Night Circus, you'll most likely enjoy this one too. If you</span>
  <span id="freeText17775871239831219327" style="display:none">Read this as part of my "Giving authors a second/last chance" challenge and...<br /><br />This is a tough one for me. <br /><br />I can acknowledge that Morgenstern’s writing is whimsical but after two books by her leaving me confused and unsatisfied, I have to admit her books are simply not for me.<br /><br />The worlds she creates are fascinating but I don't find myself caring enough about the story in them nor the characters. Frankly, I felt bored.<br /><br />If you've enjoyed The Night Circus, you'll most likely enjoy this one too. If you didn't, I would skip it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17775871239831219327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2678034392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2678034392" />
    <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads"><img alt="Amy Imogene Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548082309p2/84702001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2678034392?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Imogene Reads" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads">Amy Imogene Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=great-worldbuilding">great-worldbuilding</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2678034392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5717423367407171632">This is a masterpiece. This is flawless. This is the kind of book that comes along once in a decade. This cracks the foundations. <br/><br/><b>Imagery:</b> ★★★★★ <br/><b>Concepts:</b> ★★★★★ <br/><b>Writing:</b> ★★★★★ <br/><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★★<br/><br/>Erin Morgenstern is not for everyone. Her writing is for those who love the story for the sake of the story. <b>The lyrical, meandering, and existential prose is not the standard format, and it takes no prisoners.</b> If it's not for you, it's not for you. <br/><br/>Normally, I try to make some sort of sense in my review. Talk </span>
  <span id="freeText5717423367407171632" style="display:none">This is a masterpiece. This is flawless. This is the kind of book that comes along once in a decade. This cracks the foundations. <br /><br /><b>Imagery:</b> ★★★★★ <br /><b>Concepts:</b> ★★★★★ <br /><b>Writing:</b> ★★★★★ <br /><b>Pacing:</b> ★★★★<br /><br />Erin Morgenstern is not for everyone. Her writing is for those who love the story for the sake of the story. <b>The lyrical, meandering, and existential prose is not the standard format, and it takes no prisoners.</b> If it's not for you, it's not for you. <br /><br />Normally, I try to make some sort of sense in my review. Talk about the characters, the plot, the atmosphere. <i>The Starless Sea</i> is too close to my heart to describe accurately. (<b>What more can I say about it than what it says about itself?</b>)<br /><br />It's about <b>a subterranean library living labyrinthine space</b> where the stories are often books, but not always.<br /><br />Time and Fate are characters with an eternal love affair, but Fate was cursed to unravel over and over. <b>Sometimes, Fate can put itself back together again. Time is always waiting</b>. <br /><br /><b>Zachary Ezra Rawlins is the son of a fortune teller</b>, and he discovers that his story has been fated since the moment he saw his door to the Starless Sea years ago. He didn't open the door then, but your story has a way of finding you even when you're not aware of its presence. <br /><br /><i>The Starless Sea</i> is about metaphorical pirates, the Moon and her lover, Fate and Time, the power of the story, the cycle of beginnings and endings, owls, and bees. It has stories within stories, and perspectives that shift within the construct of time. <br /><br />I loved it. I can't wait to read it again. As Morgenstern said in an interview, <b>if <i>The Night Circus</i> embodied the concept of fall, <i>The Starless Sea</i> embodies the concept of winter.</b> She says she's going to conceptualize spring for her next one...and I'm dying to read it. <br /><br />Morgenstern, tell me a tale.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.amyimogenereads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/amyimogenereads/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5717423367407171632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781910701454" href="/book/show/42730332-the-starless-sea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=favs">favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61624004-amy?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2616158663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8250603823639804392"><b>Reading an <i>Erin Morgenstern</i> book is like dreaming with your eyes open.</b> There's something so profoundly beautiful about <i>The Starless Sea</i> that I don't really know how to put into words, but I'm going to try regardless, because if I can make even one person give this book a chance, I have accomplished my mission.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Strange, isn’t it? To love a book. When the words on the pages become so precious that they feel like part of your own history because they are.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>This book tells the story of Zachary Ez</span>
  <span id="freeText8250603823639804392" style="display:none"><b>Reading an <i>Erin Morgenstern</i> book is like dreaming with your eyes open.</b> There's something so profoundly beautiful about <i>The Starless Sea</i> that I don't really know how to put into words, but I'm going to try regardless, because if I can make even one person give this book a chance, I have accomplished my mission.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Strange, isn’t it? To love a book. When the words on the pages become so precious that they feel like part of your own history because they are.”</i>
</blockquote><br>This book tells the story of Zachary Ezra Rawlins (I mean, that's already the best name ever), who is an ordinary book nerd like you and I. One day, he stumbles upon a peculiar book, and as he reads on, he realizes that the story is about <i>him</i>. So, like any ordinary person who secretly craves an adventure to escape their bland, plain regular people life - he's up and away, going on a journey to find out what is the case with this mysterious discovery and determined to visit the <b>Starless Sea</b>, the place that his own story seems to lead him to.<br><br><b>Oh, how beautiful and heart-shattering it is, to love a book this deeply.</b> Parting with it was an overly sorrowful experience. Even though I thought <i>Erin Morgenstern</i> did everything wonderfully, I ended the book sobbing like a teenage girl after their first heartbreak. Have you ever read words so beauteous they made you cry? Anyone who can do that, who can make you feel so devoutly just by giving you words on a paper, has become a master at their craft.<br><br>Yes, the story takes some time to unfold, and yes, it may be confusing - but the purpose of this book is to draw you in slowly and reward you for your patience at the very end. For when everything falls so satisfyingly into place. If you're looking for something that you're reading for the purpose of being entertained at all times - <i>The Starless Sea</i> may not be for you. Because its strong suits are the writing and the tenderly crafted characters. This book is supposed to be for <i>Logophiles</i>, for lovers of words. If you can't appreciate the book for its writing but base it on action alone - you might find yourself lost in the tangles of words and stories here.<br><br><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579956073i/28839214._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">incredible fanart by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508-may" rel="nofollow noopener">May</a>, thank you for letting me use it ✨</blockquote><br><b>This book will stay with me forever not only because I'm a reader but because I'm a dreamer, too.</b> <i>The Starless Sea</i> feels like an ode to people like me. People that want to believe in magic and can't be satisfied with everything that is <i>ordinary</i>. People that are looking, desperately, for their own door they can escape through, every day. People that will never lose hope that their own adventure is still out there, waiting for them. People that secretly believe that they are meant for something greater, something special, something that is the opposite of normal. <br><br>I will forever thank writers like <i>Erin Morgenstern</i> for making me feel like I belong. For creating characters I can find bits and pieces of myself in. For giving me a chance to escape my dull reality, at least for some time. For giving me the opportunity to go on adventures, though they may not fully be mine, until I can find my own one day. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Not all stories speak to all listeners, but all listeners can find a story that does, somewhere, sometime. In one form or another.”</i>
  <blockquote>
    <blockquote>
      <blockquote>
        <blockquote>🔑🐝🗡</blockquote>
      </blockquote>
    </blockquote>
  </blockquote>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_3031371752" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3031371752" />
    <a title="Justin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2795921-justin"><img alt="Justin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528849864p2/2795921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3031371752?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin" href="/user/show/2795921-justin">Justin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3031371752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2482503217034889561">When I started reading The Starless Sea, I was blown away. I read through stories of pirates and girls in forests, of key holders and sword sellers, Fate, Time, the Moon, and some dude named Zach. The stories were intoxicating, like I was floating around in some hypnotic, dream-like daze, breathing in all of these beautiful short stories. They were beautifully written, imaginative little pieces of art, all smushed together and delicately held in place. <br/><br/>But somewhere in my drunken haze, the magic</span>
  <span id="freeText2482503217034889561" style="display:none">When I started reading The Starless Sea, I was blown away. I read through stories of pirates and girls in forests, of key holders and sword sellers, Fate, Time, the Moon, and some dude named Zach. The stories were intoxicating, like I was floating around in some hypnotic, dream-like daze, breathing in all of these beautiful short stories. They were beautifully written, imaginative little pieces of art, all smushed together and delicately held in place. <br /><br />But somewhere in my drunken haze, the magic started to slowly melt away. It felt kind of like when the cops show up to your college party or when you visit Chuck E. Cheese as an adult. The fun and games just kind of disappeared all of a sudden, and it ultimately became more of a chore to finish rather than a magic carpet ride, or a trip to a Wonderland, or... whatever. <br /><br />In my humble opinion, the overarching storyline of Zachary Evans Whoever that anchors this whole thing just was not very good compared to the short stories surrounding it. I loved the short stories and watching them suddenly start to connect or weave into the larger one, but when I started losing interest in Zachary’s story, I also started caring less about the other stories, too. Everything just started to unravel for me. There honestly wasn’t much of a plot underneath all the layers of stories, and the plot that was there became less and less interesting to me over time. <br /><br />There was a lot of time dedicated to painting a scene. There were beautiful descriptions of places, but not enough time dedicated to the characters. I just didn’t feel invested in the story as a whole, and enjoyed the shorter fantasy tales much more. Maybe if this was a book of fairy tales it would have worked better for me. The writing is excellent, but the overall story just didn’t connect for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2482503217034889561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3114068936" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3114068936" />
    <a title="Melissa ~ Bantering Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33853154-melissa-bantering-books"><img alt="Melissa ~ Bantering Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584398324p2/33853154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3114068936?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ~ Bantering Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ~ Bantering Books" href="/user/show/33853154-melissa-bantering-books">Melissa ~ Bantering Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33853154-melissa-bantering-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3114068936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17101906840355983445"><b>How I wish I could visit the Starless Sea.</b><br/><br/>I wish I had my own magical door; one that would allow entrance to the labyrinthine libraries of this magical underground world that Erin Morgenstern has created, where I could wander aimlessly for a time and be surrounded by books, secret rooms, riddles, and CATS. Lots and lots of cats. <br/><br/>It would be such a wonderful escape. And then once satiated, I could return to my beloved normal life and carry on . . . anxiously awaiting my next visit to the Starless</span>
  <span id="freeText17101906840355983445" style="display:none"><b>How I wish I could visit the Starless Sea.</b><br /><br />I wish I had my own magical door; one that would allow entrance to the labyrinthine libraries of this magical underground world that Erin Morgenstern has created, where I could wander aimlessly for a time and be surrounded by books, secret rooms, riddles, and CATS. Lots and lots of cats. <br /><br />It would be such a wonderful escape. And then once satiated, I could return to my beloved normal life and carry on . . . anxiously awaiting my next visit to the Starless Sea.<br /><br />Oh, how I wish.<br /><br />This wish of mine, fellow readers, is a testament to my love for this novel. <br /><br /> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43575115.The_Starless_Sea" title="The Starless Sea by Erin Morgenstern" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starless Sea</a> is exquisite. It is literary perfection. I have not felt such a deeply personal connection to a novel in quite some time, and I am now saddled with this inexplicable urge to climb to the top of the highest mountain I can find and loudly declare to the world the depth of my love for this book.<br /><br />Yes -- I love it THAT much.<br /><br /><i>The Starless Sea</i> is, quite simply, a book for book lovers. It's a beautifully written ode to fairy tales that is unlike anything I have ever read. Within its pages, there are stories within stories within stories. There are pirates, owls, magical doorways, a keeper of keys, a sculptor of stories, Fate and Time, the sun and the moon . . . and video games, of all things . . . <br /><br />( . . . and cats . . . don't forget the cats . . . )<br /><br /> . . . and there is also Zachary Ezra Rawlins, who, over the course of the novel, you will come to know and to love as you follow him on his journey to the Starless Sea. <br /><br />I will stop here and refrain from revealing any further details about the story. To do so, I think, would only serve to diminish the reading experience. <br /><br />Before diving into the book, however, you should know that <i>The Starless Sea</i> requires patience. It is not a novel to be read quickly, as every sentence is important and laced with meaning. Morgenstern takes her time and slowly unfurls the plot to the reader, chapter by chapter . . . page by page.<br /><br />And many readers struggle with the novel because of this. Very little of the story is revealed in the beginning, and Morganstern doesn't communicate the end goal or the purpose of the story AT ALL. You don't understand what Zachary is trying to accomplish in the Starless Sea, why he is on this journey, what he needs to do. It's all a mystery. You are left in the dark. And I believe this is why so many readers are unable to enjoy the book.<br /><br />But the mystery of the story is purposeful. It's intentional. Morgenstern even tells us as much within the first 100 pages of the book. (Page 66, to be exact.) And for all of the gamers out there, this is where video games come into play --<br /><br /><i>"[Zachary] doesn't always wish that real life were more like video games, but in certain situations it would be helpful. Go here. Talk to this person. Feel like you're making progress even though you don't know what it is you're trying to do, exactly."</i><br /><br />Ding! Ding! Ding! Morgenstern wrote <i>The Starless Sea</i> to be read as one would play a <i>video game</i> --you read it, progress your way through it, and know that you will not have any idea of what Zachary is trying to accomplish. Understanding this is the key to unlocking the magic of the novel.<br /><br />And I will admit -- the story is confusing. It is so intricately plotted and so tightly written that it can feel overwhelming to mentally process it all. <br /><br />Plus, in between every chapter of Zachary's story is a separate, gorgeously written fairy tale, of sorts. And you're reading all of these short little tales and wondering whether they are important and how it all fits together and -- yeah, it's a lot.<br /><br />BUT.<br /><br />If you can sit back, lose yourself in the beauty of the words, not worry about what outcome you're supposed to be reading towards, and have faith that it all will come together in the end (which it so masterfully does!), then I fully believe you will love <i>The Starless Sea</i> as much as I do.<br /><br />If you are unable to do all of the above, however, then unfortunately, it will not be the book for you. And that breaks my heart. <br /><br />Because <i>The Starless Sea</i> is a novel that should not be missed. It's so, SO wonderful. It's a fantastical masterpiece with seeping pages of magic -- pages that are patiently awaiting their chance to whisk you away to another world. <br /> <br />A world that I plan to revisit again and again . . . as I now have a new, most favorite novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17101906840355983445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2588121397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2588121397" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2588121397?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=magical-libraries">magical-libraries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2588121397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6114516827030933270"><i>"An inn that once sat at one crossroads now rests at another, ... somewhere deeper and darker where few will ever find it, by the shores of the Starless Sea."</i><br/><br/>I just think that perhaps Erin Morgenstern isn't the author for me. Does she write well? <i>Yes</i>. But do her books interest me? I'm sad to say that the answer is <i>no</i>. Both books that I've picked up from her had <i>AMAZING</i> synopses. But the plots just <b>fell flat</b>. Admittedly, this book has a much faster plot than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9361589.The_Night_Circus' title='The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Night Circus</a>, but I just wasn't in</span>
  <span id="freeText6114516827030933270" style="display:none"><i>"An inn that once sat at one crossroads now rests at another, ... somewhere deeper and darker where few will ever find it, by the shores of the Starless Sea."</i><br /><br />I just think that perhaps Erin Morgenstern isn't the author for me. Does she write well? <i>Yes</i>. But do her books interest me? I'm sad to say that the answer is <i>no</i>. Both books that I've picked up from her had <i>AMAZING</i> synopses. But the plots just <b>fell flat</b>. Admittedly, this book has a much faster plot than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9361589.The_Night_Circus" title="The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern" rel="nofollow noopener">The Night Circus</a>, but I just wasn't invested in this mystery surrounding a magical library. I just wanted <i>MORE</i>.<br /><br /><b>Zachary Ezra Rawlins</b> reminded me of a much less-interesting <i>Lazlo Strange</i> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_" title="Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Strange the Dreamer</a>. He simply loved books (and video games) and I could feel his passion for stories <i>oozing</i> through the pages. But at the end of the day, he was a bit of a <b>flat character</b>. Much like some of Neil Gaiman's characters, he was thrust into an extraordinary situation and essentially just <b>went through the motions</b> of an adventure. He didn't make many decisions of his own, but rather just went with the flow of what everyone else told him to do or was currently doing. He was a <b>tag-along</b>. <br /><br />His romance with Dorian was cute, albeit a tad lacklustre due to the unbelievably slowest of slow-burns and <b>instalove</b> (so yes, this is a cute <i>gay romance</i>). In fact, they have barely any interaction. One minute they meet, and the next, they're in love. <br /><br />But my main issue was the <b>plot</b>. There was one overarching plot with a variety of smaller subplots about <b>pirates and princesses</b>, etc. If I'm being honest, I want spinoffs of <i>THOSE</i> stories. I was much more fascinated about those stories and counted the pages for the next one to appear. Zachary's story just wasn't as interesting to me.<br /><br />If you like the <i>Night Circus</i>, you'll probably enjoy this, too. It has all the elements of an Erin Morgenstern novel, plus an <b>ode to bibliophiles</b> that all of us can relate to. I certainly loved all the references to <i>classic works of literature</i>. While it was a good story, I'm afraid that it was only an <b>average, but enjoyable</b>, read for me. I can't see it being that memorable years, or even months, from now. I want to say that I can't wait for her next release, but considering how <b>lukewarm</b> I feel about both of her novels, I can't say for certain that I'd actually pick it up, considering the density of my current TBR pile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6114516827030933270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3668454553045681778" style="display:none">I’m so sad to have not liked this book. I’ve read so many amazing reviews of it and had such high hopes. But alas, this was not my cup of tea. Swords. Bees. Books. Keys. Painted doors. Sea of honey. Owl king. Fate. The moon. Fortune Tellers. Cats. Is it an alternate reality? Is it the inside of a book? Is it the inside of a crazed mind? Is it magic? Is it aliens? I. Don’t. Know. 🤦🏼‍♀️ I held out hope all the way through that something would finally click for me... that I’d have a mind blown moment of ‘ahhh-haaaaa!!’ I get it and it’s fantastic! Unfortunately that just didn’t happen for me. 🤷🏼‍♀️ I honestly couldn’t wait for it to be over. It’s not the worst thing I’ve read. It has some spots but of intrigue. Overall I guess I lack the imagination to appreciate the sporadic whimsy this book offers. </span>

<div id="review_2588653753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2588653753" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2588653753?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2018</a>
